</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">Islam</a></td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:Green; width:2%; overflow: hidden;">&#160; </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2%</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>The principal religion in Equatorial Guinea is Christianity which is the faith of 93% of the population. These are predominately <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Roman Catholicism in Equatorial Guinea">Roman Catholic</a> (87%) while a minority are Protestants (5%). 2% of the population follows <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">Islam</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni" class="mw-redirect">Sunni</a>). The remaining 5% practise <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bahá'í Faith in Equatorial Guinea">Bahá'í Faith</a>, and other beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Health in Equatorial Guinea">Health in Equatorial Guinea</a></div>
<p>Equatorial Guinea’s innovative malaria control programs have had a remarkable impact on malaria infection, disease, and mortality in the population.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Their program consists of twice-yearly indoor residual spraying (IRS), the introduction of artemisinin combination treatment (ACTs), the use of intermittent preventive treatment in pregnant women (IPTp) and the introduction of very high coverage with long-lasting insecticide treated mosquito nets (LLINs). Their efforts resulted in a reduction in all-cause under-five mortality from 152 to 55 deaths per 1,000 live births (down 64%); and the drop occurred rapidly and timed directly with the beginning of the program.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014 there were four cases of <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a> reported, the country's first outbreak of the disease.<sup id="cite_ref-EquatorialGuinea_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EquatorialGuinea-84"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Education in Equatorial Guinea">Education in Equatorial Guinea</a></div>
<p>Under the regime of Francisco Macias, education had been significantly neglected with few children receiving any type of education. Under President Obiang, the illiteracy rate dropped from 73% to 13%<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> and the number of primary school students has risen from 65,000 in 1986 to more than 100,000 in 1994. Education is free and compulsory for children between the ages of 6 and 14.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-56"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Equatorial Guinea government has also partnered with <a href="/wiki/Hess_Corporation" title="Hess Corporation">Hess Corporation</a> and The Academy for Educational Development (AED) to establish a $20 million education program through which primary school teachers participate in a training program to teach modern child development techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> There are now 51 Model Schools. It is hoped the active pedagogy in the Model Schools will be a national reform.</p>
<p>In recent years, with change in economic/political climate and government social agendas, several cultural dispersion and literacy organizations are now located in the country, founded chiefly with the financial support of the Spanish government. The country has one university, the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Nacional_de_Guinea_Ecuatorial" title="Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial" class="mw-redirect">Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial</a> (UNGE) with a campus in Malabo and a Faculty of Medicine located in Bata on the mainland. In 2009 the university produced the first 110 national doctors.<sup id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-51"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bata Medical School is supported principally by the government of Cuba and staffed by Cuban medical educators and physicians. However, it is predicted that Equatorial Guinea will have enough national doctors in the country to be self-sufficient within the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-www1.voanews.com_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www1.voanews.com-51"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/300px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" width="300" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/450px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/600px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1792" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The port of <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>,</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Culture of Equatorial Guinea">Culture of Equatorial Guinea</a></div>
<p>In June 1984, the First Hispanic-African Cultural Congress was convened to explore the cultural identity of Equatorial Guinea. The congress constituted the center of integration and the marriage of the Hispanic culture with African cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-56"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">Media and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Media in Equatorial Guinea" class="mw-redirect">Media in Equatorial Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea">Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea</a></div>
<p>The principal means of communication within Equatorial Guinea are three state-operated <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio" class="mw-redirect">FM radio</a> stations. <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_France_Internationale" title="Radio France Internationale">Radio France Internationale</a> and Gabon-based Africa No 1 broadcast on FM in Malabo. There are also five <a href="/wiki/Shortwave" title="Shortwave" class="mw-redirect">shortwave</a> radio stations. Television Nacional, the television network, is state operated.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The international TV programme RTVGE is available via satellites in Africa, Europa, and the Americas and worldwide via Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyngsat_TVGE_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyngsat_TVGE-87"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> There are two newspapers and two magazines.</p>
<p>Equatorial Guinea ranks at position 161 out of 179 countries in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> press freedom index. The watchdog says the national broadcaster obeys the orders of the information ministry. A "news blackout" was imposed on reporting of uprisings in Arab states in North Africa in 2011, according to the Committee to Protect Journalists. Most of the media companies practice heavy <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">self-censorship</a>, and are banned by law from criticising public figures. The state-owned media and the main private radio station are under the directorship of the president's son, Teodor Obiang.</p>
<p>Landline telephone penetration is low, with only two lines available for every 100 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> There is one <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> mobile telephone operator, with coverage of <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">Bata</a>, and several mainland cities.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, approximately 40% of the population subscribed to mobile telephone services.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> The only telephone provider in Equatorial Guinea is Orange.</p>
<p>There were more than 42,000 internet users by December 2011.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Music of Equatorial Guinea">Music of Equatorial Guinea</a></div>
<p>There is little <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> coming out of Equatorial Guinea. Pan-African styles like <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> are popular, as are <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>. Acoustic guitar bands based on a Spanish model are the country's best-known indigenous popular tradition.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea national football team">Equatorial Guinea national football team</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea women's national football team">Equatorial Guinea women's national football team</a></div>
<p>Equatorial Guinea was chosen to co-host the <a href="/wiki/2012_African_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 African Cup of Nations" class="mw-redirect">2012 African Cup of Nations</a> in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, and hosted the <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">2015 edition</a>. The country was also chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/2008_Women%27s_African_Football_Championship" title="2008 Women's African Football Championship" class="mw-redirect">2008 Women's African Football Championship</a>, which they won. The <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea women's national football team">women's national team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 World Cup</a> in Germany.</p>
<p>Equatorial Guinea is famous for the swimmers <a href="/wiki/Eric_Moussambani" title="Eric Moussambani">Eric Moussambani</a>, nicknamed "Eric the Eel",<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paula_Barila_Bolopa" title="Paula Barila Bolopa">Paula Barila Bolopa</a>, "Paula the Crawler", who had astoundingly slow times at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[giˈnea ekwatoˈɾjal]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Es-guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" title="File:Es-guinea ecuatorial.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/15/Es-guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-guinea ecuatorial.ogg">listen</a>)</small></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Local pronunciation:</span>

<li id="cite_note-GEpress_noticia134es-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GEpress_noticia134es_76-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.guineaecuatorialpress.com/noticia.php?id=134&amp;lang=es">Oficina de Información y Prensa de Guinea Ecuatorial, Ministerio de Información, Cultura y Turismo</a>: <i><span lang="es">El Español es la lengua oficial administrativa y de enseñanza.
